	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">TransPennine Express</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">British train operating company owned by FirstGroup operating the TransPennine Express franchise</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the train operating company operated from 1 April 2016. For the previous franchise operator, see <a href="/wiki/First_TransPennine_Express" title="First TransPennine Express">First TransPennine Express</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>TransPennine Express</b> (legally known as First Transpennine Express Ltd) , often abbreviated to <b>TPE</b>, is a British <a href="/wiki/Train_operating_company" title="Train operating company">train operating company</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/FirstGroup" title="FirstGroup">FirstGroup</a> operating the TransPennine Express franchise. It runs regional and <a href="/wiki/Inter-city_rail_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Inter-city rail in the United Kingdom">intercity</a> rail services between the major cities of <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> and Scotland.
</p><p>The franchise operates all its services to and through <a href="/wiki/Manchester_station_group" title="Manchester station group">Manchester</a> covering three main routes. The service provides rail links for major towns and cities such as <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough" title="Middlesbrough">Middlesbrough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>.
</p><p>TransPennine Express runs trains 24 hours a day, including through New Year's Eve night. Trains run between <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> at least every three hours every night of the week. The franchise operates 51 three-carriage <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_multiple_unit" title="Diesel multiple unit">diesel</a> units and 10 four-carriage <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_350" title="British Rail Class 350">Class 350</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric</a> units. It is planned most of the fleet will be replaced by 45 new-built five-carriage units by the end of 2019, in addition to retaining a number of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> DMUs.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png/330px-TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png/495px-TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png/660px-TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="631" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TPE_passenger_journeys_2019.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Passenger journeys on the Transpennine franchise from 2010-11 to 2018-19.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The TransPennine Express brand was launched in the early 1990s by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Regional_Railways" title="Regional Railways">Regional Railways</a> sector.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It became part of Regional Railways North East and on 2 March 1997 was <a href="/wiki/Privatisation_of_British_Rail" title="Privatisation of British Rail">privatised</a> with Northern Spirit and its successor, <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Trains_Northern" title="Arriva Trains Northern">Arriva Trains Northern</a> maintaining the brand.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Rail_Authority" title="Strategic Rail Authority">Strategic Rail Authority</a> announced that it planned to reorganise the North West Regional Railways and Regional Railways North East franchises operated by <a href="/wiki/First_North_Western" title="First North Western">First North Western</a> and Arriva Trains Northern. A TransPennine Express franchise would be created for the long-distance regional services, the remaining services being operated by a new <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Rail">Northern franchise</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2003, the TransPennine franchise was awarded to a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> between <a href="/wiki/FirstGroup" title="FirstGroup">FirstGroup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keolis" title="Keolis">Keolis</a>, and the services operated by Arriva Trains Northern and First North Western were transferred to <a href="/wiki/First_TransPennine_Express" title="First TransPennine Express">First TransPennine Express</a> on 1 February 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> On 11 November 2007, the services from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester</a> to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow</a> via the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> formerly operated by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_CrossCountry" title="Virgin CrossCountry">Virgin CrossCountry</a> were transferred to First TransPennine Express.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> announced FirstGroup, Keolis/<a href="/wiki/Go-Ahead_Group" title="Go-Ahead Group">Go-Ahead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Group" title="Stagecoach Group">Stagecoach</a> had been shortlisted to bid for the next franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In December 2015, FirstGroup was awarded the franchise with TransPennine Express taking over on 1 April 2016. The franchise will run until 31 March 2023 with an option to extend for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of a recasting of the franchise map by the Department for Transport, services from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool North</a>, Manchester Airport to <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow in Furness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxenholme_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxenholme railway station">Oxenholme</a> to <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a> were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern franchise</a> on 1 April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span id="North_TransPennine"></span><span id="South_TransPennine"></span><span id="TransPennine_North_West"></span>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The TransPennine Express routes are subdivided into three operations:
</p>
<ul><li><i>North TransPennine</i>, which includes all routes that pass through the core section between Manchester and Leeds;</li>
<li><i>Anglo-Scottish</i>, which consists of services on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>;</li>
<li><i>South TransPennine</i>, which includes services running on the <a href="/wiki/Hope_Valley_line" title="Hope Valley line">Hope Valley line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Humberside_Main_Line" title="South Humberside Main Line">South Humberside Main Line</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Details of each route, including maps and timetables, are on the TransPennine Express official website <i>(see <a href="#External_links">External links</a>, below)</i>. In May 2018, following the transfer of the Manchester to Huddersfield Northern stopping service to TPE, regular services ceased between some of the intermediate Pennine stations, most daytime services either stopped at Mossley and Slaithwaite, or Greenfield and Marsden. Following the December 2018 timetable change, however, regular services resumed between Marsden and Slathwaite.
</p><p>The following services run regularly, Mondays to Saturdays (Sunday service is similar except where noted), with frequencies in <b>trains per hour</b> (tph):
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_services">Future services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Future services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Trains from Liverpool-Newcastle will extend to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh</a> via the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>, calling at Morpeth and giving 2tph from Leeds-Edinburgh together with an hourly <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> service from December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-TPEnewfranchise_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TPEnewfranchise-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Direct <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a> to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow</a> services via the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> are expected to be reintroduced at the December 2019 timetable change.<sup id="cite_ref-TPEnewfranchise_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TPEnewfranchise-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Also at the December 2019 timetable change, the current Manchester Airport to Middlesbrough service will be extended to run to and from <a href="/wiki/Redcar_Central_railway_station" title="Redcar Central railway station">Redcar Central</a> on an hourly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>TransPennine Express inherited a fleet of four <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_170" title="British Rail Class 170">Class 170</a> and 51 <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> DMUs as well as ten <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_350" title="British Rail Class 350">Class 350/4</a> EMUs from First Keolis TransPennine Express, although the Class 170s left for <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Railways" title="Chiltern Railways">Chiltern Railways</a> to be converted to <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_168" title="British Rail Class 168">Class 168s</a> shortly afterwards. After the new rolling stock has been delivered, 22 Class 185 units will be returned to <a href="/wiki/Eversholt_Rail_Group" title="Eversholt Rail Group">Eversholt Rail Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tfgmpresentation_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tfgmpresentation-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> whilst the Class 350s are due to transfer to <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_Trains" title="West Midlands Trains">West Midlands Trains</a> after the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_397" title="British Rail Class 397">Class 397</a> units enter service in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_fleet">Current fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Current fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managed_stations">Managed stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Managed stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>TransPennine Express services run over a large area of northern England and southern <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Lowlands" title="Scottish Lowlands">Scottish Lowlands</a>. Many of the largest stations they serve are managed by other train operating companies or <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.
</p><p>TransPennine Express manages the following 19 stations:<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barnetby_railway_station" title="Barnetby railway station">Barnetby</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brough_railway_station" title="Brough railway station">Brough</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cleethorpes_railway_station" title="Cleethorpes railway station">Cleethorpes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dewsbury_railway_station" title="Dewsbury railway station">Dewsbury</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_railway_station" title="Grimsby Town railway station">Grimsby Town</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull Paragon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malton_railway_station" title="Malton railway station">Malton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northallerton_railway_station" title="Northallerton railway station">Northallerton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_railway_station" title="Scunthorpe railway station">Scunthorpe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seamer_railway_station" title="Seamer railway station">Seamer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Selby_railway_station" title="Selby railway station">Selby</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yarm_railway_station" title="Yarm railway station">Yarm</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stalybridge_railway_station" title="Stalybridge railway station">Stalybridge</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thirsk_railway_station" title="Thirsk railway station">Thirsk</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thornaby_railway_station" title="Thornaby railway station">Thornaby</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Some stations from the former TransPennine Express franchise (First Keolis) were transferred to <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>. These include <a href="/wiki/Arnside_railway_station" title="Arnside railway station">Arnside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness_railway_station" title="Barrow-in-Furness railway station">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birchwood_railway_station" title="Birchwood railway station">Birchwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burneside_railway_station" title="Burneside railway station">Burneside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnforth_railway_station" title="Carnforth railway station">Carnforth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grange-over-Sands_railway_station" title="Grange-over-Sands railway station">Grange-over-Sands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendal_railway_station" title="Kendal railway station">Kendal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staveley_railway_station" title="Staveley railway station">Staveley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulverston_railway_station" title="Ulverston railway station">Ulverston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere_railway_station" title="Windermere railway station">Windermere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT270215_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT270215-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Depots">Depots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=TransPennine_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Depots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> maintains the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_350" title="British Rail Class 350">350</a> fleets at <a href="/wiki/Ardwick_train_depot" title="Ardwick train depot">Ardwick depot</a> in Manchester with a smaller facility in <a href="/wiki/York_Leeman_Road_depot" title="York Leeman Road depot">York</a>. Scottish stabling points for both stock include Corkerhill C.S.M.D. (Glasgow) and Craigentinny T.&amp;R.S.M.D. (Edinburgh). <a href="/wiki/Hitachi" title="Hitachi">Hitachi</a> will maintain the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_802" title="British Rail Class 802">AT300</a> fleet at <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Carr_rail_depot" title="Doncaster Carr rail depot">Doncaster Carr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craigentinny_TMD" title="Craigentinny TMD">Craigentinny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RGI310316_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGI310316-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  The new EMUs and loco-hauled sets will be maintained by Alstom, on behalf of TransPennine Express, at <a href="/wiki/Longsight_Electric_TMD" title="Longsight Electric TMD">Longsight</a> (Manchester), <a href="/wiki/Edge_Hill_Intercity_Depot" title="Edge Hill Intercity Depot">Edge Hill</a> (Liverpool) and <a href="/wiki/Polmadie_Traction_and_Rolling_Stock_Maintenance_Depot" class="mw-redirect" title="Polmadie Traction and Rolling Stock Maintenance Depot">Polmadie</a> (Glasgow).<sup id="cite_ref-tpe-caf_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tpe-caf-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TransPennine Express have depots for its train crews at Manchester Piccadilly, Manchester Airport (conductors), York, Newcastle, Scarborough, Hull, Cleethorpes, Sheffield, Preston, Liverpool and Glasgow Central.
</p>
